#  [](/thread/329834-dancing-with-ema)Dancing with EMA

  * [#1](/thread/329834-dancing-with-ema "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Dec 6, 2011 7:06am  Dec 6, 2011 7:06am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

Hi everybody !  
  
That 's the new simple system i'm testing since september. It looks very promising : trading EUR/USD and GBP/USD and EUR/JPY, you will see this system has been able to bring almost 2400 pips since september.  
  
All is based on price action but we need only 2 indicators :   
50 EMA, we are going to dance with her in the trend.  
5 SMA is just here to avoid range periods.  
  
TF 4H  
Let's have a look to the chart : 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 5-12-2011.jpg
Size: 86 KB](/attachment/image/849332/thumbnail?d=1365733010)](/attachment/image/849332?d=1323122751)   

  * [#2](/thread/post/5196555#post5196555 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 6, 2011 7:29am  Dec 6, 2011 7:29am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

You can see on this chart we enter short the 1st november at the open of this candle at 1.3814.  
Why ? _Because the candle before closed more than 100 pips from the EMA 50_. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 11-12-05 23 28 37.jpg
Size: 86 KB](/attachment/image/849342/thumbnail?d=1365733010)](/attachment/image/849342?d=1323124136)

  * [#3](/thread/post/5196565#post5196565 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 6, 2011 7:35am  Dec 6, 2011 7:35am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

So we sell EUR/USD at 1.3814.  
The stop loss is 100 pip ( 1.3914).  
  
Now, we are waiting, if our stop is not touched, we are going for the next step.

  * Dec 6, 2011 7:45am  Dec 6, 2011 7:45am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

The next step is selling again when the price is touching the 50 EMA, but we need at least 80 pips between this level and the previous sell order.  
  
So we sell again at 1.3726 the 11 november.  
Our stop loss is 100 pips (1.3826)  
The stop loss for the first order is also moved to 1.3826

The 18 november, we sell again at 1.3594 and all our SL are moved to 1.3694.

  * [#8](/thread/post/5196624#post5196624 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 6, 2011 8:19am  Dec 6, 2011 8:19am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

Because the last candle closed more than 100 pips above the 50 EMA, we buy at the open of the next candle at 1.3516 with a SL at 1.3416.  
  
Unfortunately, the SL is touched.  
  
Since 1st december, we had no signal to buy or to sell, because no candle closed more than 100 pips from 50 EMA. We are in a range, and only the trend is good for us.  
  
If the 5 SMA is going up and down crossing several times the 50 EMA, that a good signal to go to the beach or for some shopping... We can avoid range period ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

> 
> Disliked
> 
> Zubulon thx for posting your system i have set up my charts 3 prs and will trade along,keep us informed of possible entrys so we can follow along.  
>  From my understanding the stoploss is 100 pips and the 2nd 3rd entries have to be at least 80 pips lower from previous entry,always keeping your stop 100 pips behind the price.  
>  Is this correct...  
>  Regards
> 
> Ignored

The stoploss for all the orders is 100 pips from the last order. It is not a trailing stop. That means we will loose 100 pips for the last order. That's the price to pay to go further.

  * [#22](/thread/post/5207368#post5207368 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 9, 2011 4:15am  Dec 9, 2011 4:15am 

  * [ Spinemaligna](spinemaligna)

  * | Joined Dec 2011  | Status: Trader | [3 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=209186)

First post here so please bear with me.  
  
Having had a quick look at this system I found that quite often the price didn't make it back to the 50 EMA line but it did track the EMA + or - 100.   
I looked at taking as the trigger for the next move a crossing of the +/- line instead of the actual EMA.   
  
So I would propose entering as per post one and then wait for the price to move 80 pips. When that has happened wait for the next candle to open above/below the appropriate 100 line and move the stop down to 100 pips from this new level. This looks as though it will clean up some of the pips left on the table by the original method.  
  
I have a micro account with [FXCM](/brokers/fxcm "View FXCM Broker Profile") and will try this out in the New Year.  
  
Will keep a close eye out for any further developments.  
  
Ross

> 
> Disliked
> 
> another example with GBP/USD:  
>  10 october, we bought at 1.5618 as the previous candle closed morethan 100 pips from EMA 50.  
>  We bought again at 1.5711 and 1.5976  
>  We were stopped at 1.5876 with a global win of 323 pips.
> 
> Ignored

Hi Zebulon,  
  
thanks for your Idea on this Thread.  
I like the concept of dancing with the Emas and having not much time to follow the charts the H4 is surely an interesting alternative.  
  
I would just like to understand better your post above (actually the way to enter the trades):  
  
You mentioned to add an enter at the bounce of the EMA50, which I understand, and you normally open the trades after the close of an H4 bar (which I would prefer for not being forced to follow the price during that candle), but in the last "Buy" order was placed during the H4 candle while it actually closed way below the EMA50.  
  
So it was clearly for sure not a bounce.  
Why did you not wait for the close (and perhaps therefore avoid the losing trade) ?  
  
It is absolutely not a kind of any criticism, just really wish to better understand if I perhaps did not understand well the concept.  
  
I would like to forward test it too (and visually backtesting a bit during the weekend).  
  
Many thanks

I guess you are already short in GU as per first white arrow in the chart attached.  
  
Ema 50 is in this moment at about 80 pips above your short entry, so no SL yet.  
  
Price is approaching to Touch the Ema 50.  

  1. Will you add now a short trade (second white arrow) as soon as the price will touch the Ema 50 ?
  2. If yes, your new SL will be at 100 pips above the new entry ?
  3. The previous SL will remain at 100 pips above the first entry ?

Many thanks

The risk = stop lost = 100 pips  
It is possible when the price is far from the entry to move the sop loss to break eaven : EUR/USD we sell at 1.3264, the price is actually 1.3036, it is more than 200 pips from our entry.  
In this case, yes, i would move my stop for a free run ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

> [Quoting migmac](/thread/post/5234850#post5234850 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> at 1.5480 the price is not touching the 50 EMA as per your rules, so why did you open at this price?
> 
> Ignored

For the first entry, the rule is : when a 4H bar close more than 100 pips from the EMA 50, open a trade at the open of the next 4H bar.  
  
For the 2d, 3rd, 4th.. entry, it is when the price is touching the 50 EMA.

To the rules of the 2d, 3rd, 4th...entry:   
  
it is when the price is touching the 50 Ema _on a retrace_ , _but only if the price at the touch is at least 80 pips in positive from your entry._  
  
Is the underlined correct ?

  * Edited 5:05am  Dec 24, 2011 4:41am | Edited 5:05am 

  * [ Fair Dinkum](fair*dinkum)

  * | Joined Dec 2011  | Status: Trader | [18 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=213037)

> [Quoting zebulon](/thread/post/5244587#post5244587 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> As you can see, for me the price didn't reach 1.3200 after the sell at 1.3120
> 
> Ignored

Amazing there can be over a 30 pip difference between quote systems or brokers.  
  
So all your work is off a quote system or are you trading sim/real time?  
  
I am going to check with a couple of these spread houses and see what they come up with for that day, after Christmas.  
  
Edit: I figured out what happened.   
  
It seems that the quote system is set to indicate the closing price every four minutes, hence the close at 1.3197, BUT the price spike did actually go through to 1.3224. So if there was an order pending over 1.3197 and up to 1.3224 (stop) it would been filled.  
  
Therefore, you have been stopped out at 1.3220, unfortunately.

Ok, I just caught up with my French translation of "prix moyens", which means average price. Therefore, I have to assume the close of the bar in question was the AVERAGE of that period, being 1.3197, but in reality, the price WENT through TO 1.3224 .   
  
The truth of the matter, is I was also long ES mini and waited in abated breathe that I was going to get stopped at 1.3233 in my 6E trade in the fast market conditions at the time.I lucked out.  
  
But,that knocked out your "stop" at 1.3220.  
  
Maybe, it could be worth your while to set up a demo account to help with entry and exit points.

  * [#97](/thread/post/5248281#post5248281 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 27, 2011 6:50am  Dec 27, 2011 6:50am 

  * [ APeng](apeng)

  * | Joined Dec 2011  | Status: Trader | [41 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=213565)

Hello Zebulon,  
thanks for sharing your strategy. I like it because it is simple and it is a trend following one ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1). I did some work and coded it for MetaTrader to do backtests for a longer time period.  
  
That is the result from January 2008 to December 2011 **WITHOUT** taking care about if we are in a trending market or not. If a candle closes 100 pips or more away from the EMA 50 (H4) a trade is entered and the following trades are entered when the EMA 50 is touched and we are at least 80 pips away from the previous trades entry. The SL is also set as described to 100 pips away from the last trades entry for all trades.  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...1&d=1324936463](http://www.forexfactory.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=863454&stc=1&d=1324936463)  
There are periods where we gain big profit but most is given away again because we entered the market and no trend began.  
  
Now i included the EMA 5 into the EA **to take care about whether there is a trend or not**. As a rule I defined that the initial market entry (and so the following ones, too) may only be done if the EMA 5 did not cross the EMA 50 for at least 25 candles.  
That is the result from January 2008 to December 2011:  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...1&d=1324936463](http://www.forexfactory.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=863455&stc=1&d=1324936463)  
  
What do I want to show with it?  
If you have a good trend following strategy you need to stay out of the market if there is no trend (of course). And the question is always to make out, if the market is trending or not. I think that it is a nice result if a simple rule like not to trade if the faster MA did hit the slower MA for a predefined period. And if even that one simple step makes such a difference, I would like to ask you what kind of other method could be used in addition to reach an even better result?  
  
Greetings, APeng.  
  
  
P.S. Thats my first post in this forum and I had trouble with embedding the images - I hope it worked and you dont mind that they are attached, too.

Hey mate. I observed Zebulon's strategy might be a potentially profitable one in the long run, but you have to understand it carries an arbitral risk/reward ratio. I can only advice you to demo test it on a good number of trades to get good results. If you risk 100pips to make 20pips, it only takes a single loss to wipe 5 profits. Either back+front test it to get ur good mm that fits or just let your trades run the way Zebulon prescribed. You never can tell what trade will make the big break. Period is not an excuse, who knows what the opening price of the fiber would be come 2012?...all the best to you!![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

I use Metatrader (I posted the whole backtests results for the previous tests above, so it should be obvious). I have no problems backtesting multiple timeframes with MT. But the strategy uses only one anyway. I implemented the addon trades - I simulated exactly zebulon strategy.  
  
Another thougt is to close a part of the position. Trades are often in profit area before running into SL. So if the trade is +100 pips close half of the lots and you are break even without pulling the SL to +/- zero pips. Doing that you dont have a closer SL and you are not beeing stopped out too fast and if a trend starts you are still in the market.  
  
What kind of programm would you commend instead of Metatrader?

> I use Metatrader (I posted the whole backtests results for the previous tests above, so it should be obvious). I have no problems backtesting multiple timeframes with MT. But the strategy uses only one anyway. I implemented the addon trades - I simulated exactly zebulon strategy.  
>    
>  **Another thougt is to close a part of the position.** Trades are often in profit area before running into SL. So if the trade is +100 pips close half of the lots and you are break even without pulling the SL to +/- zero pips. Doing that you dont have a closer SL...
> 
> Ignored

Nice job APeng. Keep up the good work. I backtest on metatrader too and also work with the DealBoook from GFT. But recently, GFT has removed the strategy tester from DB and I'm stuck with MT4 and Excel.  
  
Closing part of the position is a good idea but you have to know it changes the risk/reward of the strategy. Risking 100pips on 0.1 lot on a standard account gives u a $100 loss if your SL hits. To be able to close half positions, you'll need to use 0.2 lots which hands you a $200 loss if the SL hits first. This is just a case study...I'm sure you'll understand what I mean. 

Don't just beat the markets, leave bruises.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Hi all, whats the filter on this again, not really explained ?   
  
Using the 5sma for ranging periods, its indecisiveness up/down happens all the time. I use it in another system for 4 years now and know it cant be used in this way for a 4hr method (or as I see).  
So anyway along with someone else here, I coded it for MT4, it seems to be having a good run on some of the pairs lately, but doesnt stand the last 10 years. The last 3 years and youd be creamed. At best you could average out.  
  
Dont mean to sound negative, methods need to prove to me they can stand the test of time in all conditions. This reminds me of another method about 5-6 yrs back, they all got creamed too.  
I see potential so Im going to run some other filters and see what arises.

To avoid ranging periods, here is the rule :  
when 5 SMA cross 3 times 50 EMA, we don't trade before 15 new candles appears.  
Your backtest included this rule will be different ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

  * [#166](/thread/post/5294532#post5294532 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 14, 2012 7:51am  Jan 14, 2012 7:51am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

Trying to explain as best as i can....Sorry for my poor english !!  
  
To avoid periods of range, if SMA 5 cross EMA 50 3 times, you count the next candles : as you can see on the chart, the black line (SMA 5) cross the blue line (EMA 50) 3 times. After that we have 4 candles before another cross.  
4< 15 candles. go on.  
After that, we have 8 candles before another cross. 8< 15\. go on.  
After that, we have 9 candles before another cross. 9< 15\. go on.  
After that, we have more than 15 candles without a new cross,so we are waiting for a candle closing more than 100 pips from EMA 50 for an entry.  
  
I hope this could help !!

Hi, you're right, impossible to stay all day long in front of the screen !  
For the first entry, you need to check every 4 H. And sometime you don't need because the price is very far from EMA 50. (I don't wake up during nights ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f634.png?v=15.1))  
For the next entries, i do the same... Every 4h when it is possible for me.  
I estimate the EMA 50 level (from one candle to the next, it doesn't move a lot) and i program a pending order.  
I think few pips from the rules entry is not a problem because we are looking for a big trend which may give us plenty of pips...  
And sometimes, you can catch a better price when you miss the entry according to the rules... it makes a balance ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

  * [#188](/thread/post/5303677#post5303677 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 18, 2012 9:23am  Jan 18, 2012 9:23am 

  * [ ejohnston5](ejohnston5)

  * | Joined Oct 2010  | Status: Trader | [72 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=157511)

Taken from some other threads such as Profit All Day System or the Trading Made Simple Thread, to address ranging periods you may want to consider banding the 50 EMA with the 50 EMA high and 50 EMA low averages. Or look at using 50 EMA Envelopes at around 0.3% to 0.5%. These will basically create a "no mans land" band around the 50 EMA. As the 5 EMA breaks out of the "no mans land" then grab your 100 pip entry rule. Even with these, due to market volatitilty and varying average daily ranges the bands might need to be adjusted. Maybe we look at a band of the 50 EMA+/- the ATR and look for the 5 EMA to break that range on way to the 100 pip entry.  
  
I had a hard time following the 15 candle rule as it didn't seem to make sense when to take start the 15 candle clock. Sounds like if your first signal cross fails, then you wait until it crosses how ever many times again until it can spend at least 15 candles on one side of the 50 EMA. Harder to program this into an EA or indicator.  
  
I think banding the range may be a better way IMO.

ruten, you may have forgotten or been mistaken ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1) at your 1.2880 level the EMA will be higher than it is now that's why the closed candle will not be out of the EMA +-100pips channel. In this case, according to the strategy you won't be allowed to execute the buy order. As I know, the EMA depends on the candles close prices. So it varies when price is moving. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

I would like somebody to shed some light on a question I have, if somebody could help.  
  
Its about entry rules when the initial entry _after a trend change_ was missed.  
  
[](http://shrani.si/?R/ml/1D0rljuB/1.jpg)<http://shrani.si/t/R/ml/1D0rljuB/1.jpg>  
  
The 1st entry after the trend change was missed - what now?  
Do I enter at the next touch of the candle which is 40 pips below the 1st entry?  
Or do I wait for the next touch 110 pips below?  
  
And when do I enter, at the touch or 100 pips below the touch since this will be "my 1st entry" though not the 1st entry of the overall trend? 

Thoughts are things

  * Jan 25, 2012 12:16am  Jan 25, 2012 12:16am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar202652_3.gif) Quezoy](quezoy)

  * | Joined Nov 2011  | Status: Trader | [1,078 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=202652)

Tnx Zebulon.  
  
I have a suggestion. I'm trying out renko charts in the last time and applied them to your system. I've used 20 pip boxes.  
  
For the last EUR/USD trade, just looking at the pip gain from 1st entry till the end of the trade, renko would have given 400 pips, while the normal 4H gave 360 pips.  
  
[](http://shrani.si/?a/G0/x9m18lr/renko.jpg)<http://shrani.si/t/a/G0/x9m18lr/renko.jpg> [](http://shrani.si/?3o/MJ/1I0ShpdT/time.jpg)<http://shrani.si/t/3o/MJ/1I0ShpdT/time.jpg>  
  
Unfortunately I have only 2 months of data for renko, because its based on 1M charts. So I cant do more backtests.   
However, I'll try it on some forward testing from now on and see what happens.  
  
  
Another suggestion I have is not to reenter (2nd, 3rd, 4th... entry) the trade at the initial touch of the candle, but when the first candle crosses back over the EMA in the direction of the trend.   
  
This way, we dont lose the 100 pips in a situation, where the candle crossing the EMA also triggers the SL. Besides, if we wait for the cross back, this means the EMA went a bit more against the trend and therefore reenter from a better position - few more pips.  
  
[](http://shrani.si/?2M/l6/1UCjMev/1.jpg)<http://shrani.si/t/2M/l6/1UCjMev/1.jpg>

Thoughts are things

> 
> Disliked
> 
> How long should I demo trade with it before starting with real money??
> 
> Ignored

Hey Mazi in my view the demo account is like playing a Call of duty game and real account is like going to Afghanistan.  
  
You should play with the demo just to master basics and go for live asap but, Don't even think about going with more than 50$ account even 50$ is too much because you will essentially blow it as anyone else did. The key point is to trade micro lots with pennies and your reward are **points** (pips) **not the money** because greed for more and more money is behind every busted account. I knew few people who triple their demo accounts which just boosted their egos then went for real and end up on the floor. Its completely different world to play with real hard earned money because with real account you cant control your emotions. So my advice is just go for it with as smallest tiniest micro tiny lots as you can find and just trade as much as you can.

Hy Mazis12  
  
After 1 month of demo I go live and in my first day of live trading I blow off my account, 2 weeks I don`t touch forex. Till now I blow off 10 real accounts.   
  
Now I trade demo and learn technical analysis. I can suggest a good book of technical analysis:  
  
Technical Analysis of The Financial Markets - John Murphy.  
  
Regards 

Enter Signature

  * Jan 27, 2012 11:15pm  Jan 27, 2012 11:15pm 

  * [ mazis12](mazis12)

  * | Joined Jan 2012  | Status: Trader | [63 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=218157)

Hi Lame, Danutz & Zebulon,  
Thanks all of you for your kind advice.... I, also with my little experience, would like to start with little account, microlots, low leverage (1:50 or 1:100 at most... I prefer the first option though) and 1-2% risk....   
  
During trading in demo account, I also use the similar set up... I've blown up few demo accounts already.... until I found this thread.... I've also lost good deal of pips initially following this strategy (failing to use it properly)...... but now 3 positions in three pairs - 3 microlots... As lame said... I was enjoying gaining pips...   
  
I know, real world is different... when price moves opposite direction.... I can stick to the rule as it's a demo account... I think, I couldn't wait if the account would have been a real account.... so I need to develop skill and need to learn to be patient at the same time......   
  
Thanks for the advice.... This kind of support boosts up the newbies like me....

> [Quoting mazis12](/thread/post/5345958#post5345958 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Like _[Quezoy](http://www.forexfactory.com/quezoy)_ ,I was also impatient and I was about to go short... But when I read the comment from zebulon again, I found that I should wait till the candle close at more than 100 pips from 50 EMA... So I refrained myself from entering short position with a sad mindset... but at the end, I was paid off for following the rules....  
>    
>  I think, it's natural to be impatient for newbies... we should learn to be patient, whatever rules we follow.....Thanks Zebulon, you're a great help for us..
> 
> Ignored

You're wellcome !  
Yes usually we are impatient because we are used to shortest time frames as 5 or 15 min. Here one candle needs 4H to build. I think these 4H candles are more significant and we have more time.  
We don't need to have the nose on the road to drive our trades, more distance allows us a better view to control the direction ...

hi zeb  
  
pls. comment... on the entries if i were trade this pair.  
  
the big box is 100 pips the small 80.  
  
the 1st entry is the bottom line due 100 pips away from ma50.  
the 2nd entry is the top line due 80 pips away from 1st entry and touch the ma50.  
  
tq n cheers

> yes, tell us about it !

> Ignored

ok, work in progress and not exhaustively tested yet but some food for thought perhaps...  
  
Still using the EMA(50) but with the upper/lower band scaled down to 25 pips. The key seems to be the strength of the close of the signal candle, not only closing above/below the band but also near the high of the signal candle.  
  
The signal candle is then fibbed to derive SLs and target. T1 being 1:1, T2 1:2. I've also used the fib tool to show the 80% level which could be used to quickly check the strength of the close.   
  
EU and GU examples below. I'll be forward testing mainly on EU. (ignore the EU short trade in the chart; another strat.) 

Attached Image(s) (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: Thrust60GU100212.GIF
Size: 109 KB](/attachment/image/895451/thumbnail?d=1365745092)](/attachment/image/895451?d=1328859857)   
[![Click to Enlarge

Name: Thrust60090212.GIF
Size: 278 KB](/attachment/image/895452/thumbnail?d=1365745092)](/attachment/image/895452?d=1328859857)

When we are not enough patient, SL give us frustation each time they are touched. Don't forget we are looking for big moves with 5 or 6 entries which will give us plenty of pips. When little moves brings me little pips, it is good for me, i wait for the next start.  
  
Second thing, i think all the news are in the price.  
I don't need to analyse news. I just know that at 2.30 pm, we could have a move, maybe a big one, maybe up, maybe down. I don't know.  
But i know what i will do according to the price level.

so...let me check here.... EUR/USD pair, 5 SMA crossed 3 times in 8 days.... is it ranging now or what am I missing here??

I have always a stop loss 100 pips from my last order so my trades are closed on EUR/USD : from 1.2907 and 1.3055 and 1.3184, i win 106 pips.  
Not so bad and waiting for a big move. It is also night for me, so as the actual candle is not 100 pips from EMA 50 i go to sleep ! I'm not afraid when 1 or 2 candles are alive when i'm sleeping or playing tennis. That will not change a lot, especially during asian session which is not usually very strong.

> [Quoting APeng](/thread/post/5250858#post5250858 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
>   
>  Another thougt is to close a part of the position. Trades are often in profit area before running into SL. So if the trade is +100 pips close half of the lots and you are break even without pulling the SL to +/- zero pips. Doing that you dont have a closer SL and you are not beeing stopped out too fast and if a trend starts you are still in the market.  
> 
> 
> Ignored

i think this is a good idea, i will enter with 2 trades, one for running and one closed when profit is +100 pips

I removed condition "Since last entry". It is wrong.  
  
Conditions is:  
If we have 3 crosses SMA5 and EMA50 (no more than 15 candles between each cross) then we wait 15 candles.  
  
<http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-dancingema/2/fx5.png>  
  
Yes, it rescue us from range, but it has worse result:  
[http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-danc...tegyTester.htm](http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-dancingema/2/StrategyTester.htm)  
  
1\. Without SMA5, but excluded summer holidays:  
[http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-danc...tegyTester.htm](http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-dancingema/1/StrategyTester.htm)  
  
2\. With SMA5 and with summer holidays:  
[http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-danc...tegyTester.htm](http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-dancingema/2/StrategyTester.htm)  
  
3\. With SMA5 and excluded summer holidays:  
[http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-danc...tegyTester.htm](http://www.forexguns.com/fxg/bt-dancingema/3/StrategyTester.htm)  
  
Summary:  
The better is number 1 :-(

> Ignored

Hi Tom,  
  
I backtested this manually using Alpari UK and got these results from January 2011 up to last Friday...  
  
EU - +4065  
EY - +3277  
AU - +505  
  
This was using:  
  
\- 100+ close past 50 MA for EP  
\- No trade if 5 MA crossed 50 MA 3 or more times within 30 candles (if so wait 15 candles until next entry)  
\- No trade if 5 MA crossed 50 MA 2 or more times within 10 candles (if so wait 15 candles until next entry)  
  
My money management was different however to that stated by zebulon.   
  
For EU I used 2 lots for entry taking 1 lot profit at +200 at which point I move the SL to BE and letting the second lot run. If the 2nd lot hits +500 close trade. I am stopped out if the trade still runs and moves past the opposite side of 50 MA by 100 pips... I had no re-entries on a 50 MA re-touch...  
  
For EY and AU I did the same but took profit at +150 and +400...

>  This was using:  
>    
>  \- 100+ close past 50 MA for EP  
>  \- No trade if 5 MA crossed 50 MA 3 or more times within 30 candles (if so wait 15 candles until next entry)  
>  \- No trade if 5 MA crossed 50 MA 2 or more times within 10 candles (if so wait 15 candles until next entry)  
>    
>  My money management was different however to that stated by zebulon.

  * [#399](/thread/post/5405695#post5405695 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 22, 2012 1:54am  Feb 22, 2012 1:54am 

  * [ zebulon](zebulon)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [532 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=87843)

Thanks to all of you and to tom to do the best to increase this strategy !  
  
I think backtesting with an EA is a good way to find the best parameters.  
  
What i mean with the 5 SMA cross is :  
  
if EMA5 cross EMA15 three times since last loss (with no more than 15 4H candles between each EMA5 crossing EMA50), we cant entry even if others conditions apply..in that case, we have to wait for 15 4h candles before entering (if others conditions are still valid).  
  
But this rule is not writed in the stone. If backtest tells us it is better with 20 candles or 2 crosses, we will adapt...  
  
I 'm very confident with this strategy, the trend brings pips. To avoid range periods, i think 5 SMA cross rule and no opposite trade rule (if we don't go short on a pair when the 2 others are still open long) will help a lot...

  * [#429](/thread/post/5424453#post5424453 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 28, 2012 8:55am  Feb 28, 2012 8:55am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar190445_2.gif) maudur](maudur)

  * Joined Aug 2011 | Status: Trader | [583 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=190445)

Zebulon,  
  
Below are a couple of scripts that I developed to open orders for this extraordinary strategy.  
  
I prefer open 4 orders at a time, each order with a TP at a distance of 100 pips over the previous. The last order I open it with twice the TP or without TP. This script help us to open these orders with the following parameters:  
  
StopLoss: Distance in **points** for each order.  
TakeProfit: Distance in **points** for each order with respect to previous.  
Lots: Lots for each order.  
RiskPercent: Applies to calculate the maximum exposure by all orders to open about equity. Only calculated if Lots = 0.  
Orders: Number of orders to open.  
TPLastOrder: If true, the last order opens with TP.  
DistanceLastOrder: TP multiplied by this parameter to the last order. Ie, If 2 and TP = 100 pips, the TP of the last order is 200 pips.  
MagicNumber: MagicNumber of each order.  
  
If interested, please try first these scripts on a demo account.  
  
Any comments will be gladly answered. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: ex4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/ex4.gif) [Buy Dancing With EMA.ex4](/attachment/file/907773?d=1330386779) 6 KB | 492 downloads 

![File Type: ex4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/ex4.gif) [Sell Dancing With EMA.ex4](/attachment/file/907774?d=1330386779) 6 KB | 459 downloads

Why wait?  
  
The rules are very clear and when the entry parameters are present in the market you enter. Simple as that.   
  
Don't wait or try to second guess a system as you have no way of knowing what will happen next. The only thing you can do is take every trade that qualifies according to the rules - as Mark Douglas would say - "without reservation or hesitation"...

#  [](/thread/329834-dancing-with-ema)Dancing with EMA 

  * 

  * [#461](/thread/post/5468688#post5468688 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 13, 2012 1:54pm  Mar 13, 2012 1:54pm 

  * [ mazis12](mazis12)

  * | Joined Jan 2012  | Status: Trader | [63 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=218157)

> [Quoting zebulon](/thread/post/5402374#post5402374 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 1) I think EUR/USD GBP/USD and EUR/JPY are highly correlated. And we can avoid more losses and increase this strategy with this new rule : don't go short on a pair when the 2 others are still open long.  
>  The last short trade on EUR/USD would not be open with this rule.  
> 
> 
> Ignored

Now, EUR/JPY is on opposite side of EUR/USD and GBP/USD in relation to 50 EMA line. GBP/USD is on short position continuing phase, EUR/USD is moving towards 50 EMA after probable short opening position though second short entry is not probable yet as it's not 80 pips away from first entry.....rather if anyone missing the first entry can jump into the train..... EER/JPY is on continuing long position..... the picture mentioned above is considering each pair alone....   
  
now as the new rule evolved in the above mentioned post.... suppose a person has no position opened in this picture.... how should he move on.... should he plan for going short on EUR/USD or wait for all pairs going on same side of 50 EMA??  
  
I'm a learner.... learning stage... so an expert opinion could help me and all the newbie..... 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#462](/thread/post/5468728#post5468728 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:59pm  Mar 13, 2012 2:20pm | Edited 2:59pm 

  * [ mazis12](mazis12)

  * | Joined Jan 2012  | Status: Trader | [63 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=218157)

On my chart on 9th March 2012, at 1200 hours (Trading platform timezone, GMT +2), price movement of GBP/USD, EUR/USD was strong downwards (105 pips and 97 pips body of the candle respectively) where it was 10 pips downwards for EUR/JPY....   
  
now to say correlated pair, is price movement direction similarity sufficient? or the amount of price movement (in terms of pip) should be considered?? another thing is that-- at the above mentioned scenario EUR/USD was below the 50 EMA and short position was opened and EUR/JPY was above the 50 EMA and a long position was opened for that pair.... according to the rules described in the first post....and the price movement in all three cases helped to stay on the positions..... so should we avoid the correlation theory of pairs here or it's just a single incidence which should not affect the new rule....  
  
On 27th Februrary 2012 at 800 hours (GMT +2), GBP/USD moved up 1 pips, EUR/USD moved down 61 pips and EUR/JPY pips moved down 109 pips....  
  
On 29th Februrary 2012 at 1200 hours (GMT +2), GBP/USD moved up 29 pips, EUR/USD moved down 69 pips and EUR/JPY pips moved up 19 pips....  
  
On 8th March 2012 at 800 hours (GMT +2), GBP/USD moved up 38 pips, EUR/USD moved up 63 pips and EUR/JPY pips moved up 99 pips....  
  
During writing this post... GBP/USD is moving down 9 pips, EUR/USD is moving down 23 pips and EUR/USD is moving down 47 pips....  
  
I know.... price movement won't correlate in every minutes and seconds.... but I'm not looking at point of time here....just pointed the important price movement period in recent past.  
  
Price movement of almost 100 pips can trigger any buy/sell opportunity or can hit s/l...... I think, direction might be similar most cases but the speed of movement is not the same always so.... prices of all pairs are not on the same side and thus, similar position might not be possible..... Expert's opinion pls.... 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Hi all,  
  
I'm very new both to the trading and to this forum (in matter of fact this is my first post here).  
  
I found this strategy very simple and appealing but I'd like to clarify some issues with you:  
  
1) I don't quite get when you can move SL to BE. After "earning" +200 pips? Is it dependend on how many positions you have?  
  
2) What is the rationale of buying when price touch EMA 50? Eg. we are short on EUR/USD. Price goes steeply down, without retracement and never touches EMA 50. We're making some crazy pips on one position, but then we have to lose it when trend reverse? Because we don't have additional positions and our stoploss is not trailing one?  
  
3) What is exact meaning of "entry on retracement". How do we know if it's a final retracement?  
  
If anyone could help me, it would be very appreciated,  
  
best.

If you add this management, you should come out on top.   
First trade, set TP - 500 pips for four digit broker.  
Second trade tp - 400 pips and let the subsequent trade run.  
  
Note: set stop loss to -50 when trade is +150, and set stop loss to breakeven when trade is +200pips, hope this help some few traders, backtest and see for yourself.

Hi,  
  
I sent a PM to Zebulon to ask his permission to publish some modifications I made to your strategy to try to make the maximum not only in periods of trend, but avoid to the maximum, ranges.  
  
First of all congratulations to Zebulon for their strategy and I give credit to nanningbob from whom I learned a lot, especially in its strategy [Nb 10.2](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=308304) of which I have taken several things to match the strategy of Zebulon.  
  
I hope I can help in some way to all who have given me his teachings here in FF.  
  
Here are the modifications to the strategy:  
  
Indicators:  
EMA50 Shift 0 Close. (Levels +100 and -100)  
10.2W 1MA MTF 5.12  
10.2 WeeklyPivots S1.R1 5.9  
10.2 WOH 1.0 5.4  
10.2 WOH 2x1 5.4  
10.2 TMA Slope v1.4B 4.30 for EA  
  
**SELL:**  
_Entries:_ PA close below of EMA 50  100 (below of lower band of channel), and  
TMA Slope < -0.4, and  
PA < Weekly Pivot, and  
PA < Weekly Open, and  
WOH 1.0 < 0, and  
WOH 2x1 < 0  
  
SL = Upper Band of Channel. At close of each candle you should move the SL to the upper band of the channel.  
  
(*) When the PA touch again EMA50,   
If PA is at least 80 pips below the entry price of the previous order, and  
TMA Slope < -0.4, and  
WOH 1.0 < 0, and  
WOH 2x1 < 0  
Open new SELL.  
SL = Upper Band of Channel. At close of each candle you should move the SL to the upper band of the channel.  
  
Repeat (*) until close the orders for exit conditions.  
  
_Exits:_ TMA Slope > -0.4, or  
Stop Out  
  
**BUY:**  
_Entries:_ PA close above of EMA 50 + 100 (above of upper band of channel), and  
TMA Slope > 0.4, and  
PA > Weekly Pivot, and  
PA > Weekly Open, and  
WOH 1.0 > 0, and  
WOH 2x1 > 0  
  
SL = Lower Band of Channel. At close of each candle you should move the SL to the lower band of the channel.  
  
(*) When the PA touch again EMA50,   
If PA is at least 80 pips above the entry price of the previous order, and  
TMA Slope > -0.4, and  
WOH 1.0 > 0, and  
WOH 2x1 > 0  
Open new BUY.  
SL = Lower Band of Channel. At close of each candle you should move the SL to the lower band of the channel.  
  
Repeat (*) until close the orders for exit conditions.  
  
_Exits_ :TMA Slope < 0.4, or  
Stop Out  
  
**_NOTE:_** In high volatility pairs is necessary to change the distance of each band of the channel at 200 and the distance for new orders to 160. (For example, XAUUSD).  
  
**Pairs** : In all, preferred the more volatile, eg GBPNZD, EURNZD, GBPAUD, GBPCAD, GBPJPY, GBPCHF, EURUSD, EURCAD, EURAUD, GBPUSD, EURJPY, AUDUSD. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
